			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Widener Library</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>

<p>The <b>Harry Elkins Widener Memorial Library</b>, housing some 3.5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million books in its "vast and cavernous"<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-sheavian_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheavian-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stacks_(library_architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stacks (library architecture)">stacks</a>, is the center­piece of the Harvard College Libraries (the libraries of Harvard's <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Faculty_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Harvard Faculty of Arts and Sciences">Faculty of Arts and Sciences</a>) and, more broadly, of the entire <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Library" title="Harvard Library">Harvard Library</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-counting_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-counting-2">[2]</a></sup> It honors 1907 <a href="/wiki/Harvard_College" title="Harvard College">Harvard College</a> graduate and <a href="/wiki/Book_collector" class="mw-redirect" title="Book collector">book collector</a> <a href="/wiki/Harry_Elkins_Widener" title="Harry Elkins Widener">Harry Elkins Widener</a>, and was constructed by his mother <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Elkins_Widener" title="Eleanor Elkins Widener">Eleanor Elkins Widener</a> after his death in the <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_RMS_Titanic" title="Sinking of the RMS Titanic">sinking of the RMS <i>Titanic</i></a> in 1912.</p>
<p>The library's holdings, which include works in more than one hundred languages, comprise "one of the world's most comprehen­sive research collec­tions in the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_social_sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="List of social sciences">social sciences</a>."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-collections_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collections-3">[3]</a></sup> Its 57 miles (92&#160;km) of shelves, along five miles (8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>km) of aisles on ten levels, comprise a "<a href="/wiki/Labyrinth" title="Labyrinth">labyrinth</a>" which one student "could not enter without feeling that she ought to carry a compass, a sandwich, and a whistle."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-tuchman_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tuchman-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the building's heart are the <b>Widener Memorial Rooms</b>, displaying papers and mementos recalling the life and death of Harry Widener, as well as the <b>Harry Elkins Widener Collec­tion</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-hewc_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hewc-5">[5]</a></sup> "the precious group of rare and wonder­fully interesting books brought together by Mr. Widener",<sup id="cite_ref-snead_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snead-6">[6]</a></sup> to which was later added one of the few perfect <a href="/wiki/Gutenberg_Bible#Existing_copies_of_the_Gutenberg_Bible" title="Gutenberg Bible">Gutenberg Bibles</a>‍—‌the object of a 1969 burglary attempt conjectured by Harvard's police chief to have been inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Heist_film" title="Heist film">heist film</a><span style="white-space:nowrap"> </span><i><a href="/wiki/Topkapi_(film)" title="Topkapi (film)">Topkapi</a></i>.</p>
<p>Campus legends holding that Harry Widener's fate led to institu­tion of an undergrad­uate swimming-proficiency requirement, and that an additional donation from his mother subsidizes ice cream at Harvard meals, are without foundation.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:422px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg/420px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg" width="420" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg/630px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg/840px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1480" data-file-height="706" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_TabletMontage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tablets in vestibule and foyer. "This noble gift to learning comes to us with the shadow of a great sorrow resting upon it", said <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cabot_Lodge" title="Henry Cabot Lodge">Henry Cabot Lodge</a> at the dedica­tion. "But with the march of the years the shad­ow of grief will pass, while the great memo­rial will remain".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[a]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>

<h2><span id="Background,_conception_and_gift"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Background.2C_conception_and_gift">Background, conception and gift</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Widener_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background, conception and gift">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Widener_w1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eleanor Widener, son <a href="/wiki/George_D._Widener,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="George D. Widener, Jr.">George</a> <i>(l)</i>, and archi­tect <a href="/wiki/Horace_Trumbauer" title="Horace Trumbauer">Horace Trum­bauer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Yard" title="Harvard Yard">Harvard Yard</a>, <span class="nowrap">c. 1912</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Predecessor">Predecessor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Widener_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Predecessor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gore_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Gore Hall">Gore Hall</a></div>
<p>By the opening of the twentieth century alarms had been issuing for many years about Harvard's "disgrace­fully inadequate"<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-histcambridge_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-histcambridge-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:276</sup> library, Gore Hall, completed 1841 (when Harvard owned some 44,000 books)<sup id="cite_ref-bentinck1980_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bentinck1980-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:5</sup> and declared full in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-bentinck1980_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bentinck1980-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:5</sup> Librarian <a href="/wiki/Justin_Winsor" title="Justin Winsor">Justin Winsor</a> concluded his 1892 Annual Report by pleading, "I have in earlier reports exhausted the language of warning and anxiety, in represent­ing the totally inadequate accommo­da­tions for books and readers which Gore Hall affords. Each twelve months brings us nearer to a chaotic condition";<sup id="cite_ref-lib1892_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lib1892-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:15</sup> his successor <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Cary_Coolidge" title="Archibald Cary Coolidge">Archibald Cary Coolidge</a> asserted that the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Library" title="Boston Public Library">Boston Public Library</a> was a better place to write an undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Thesis" title="Thesis">thesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coolidge_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coolidge-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:29</sup> Despite substantial additions in 1876 and 1907,<sup id="cite_ref-leighton_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leighton-14">[13]</a></sup> in 1910 a committee of architects termed Gore</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>unsafe [and] unsuitable for its object<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... no amount of tinkering can make it really good<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... hopelessly over­crowded<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... leaks when there is a heavy rain<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... intolerably hot in summer<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... books are put in double rows and are not infrequently left lying on top of one another, or actually on the floor<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>...<sup id="cite_ref-bentinck1976_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bentinck1976-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:51–2</sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>With dormitory basements pressed into service as overflow storage<sup id="cite_ref-graduates_window_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graduates_window-16">[15]</a></sup> for Harvard's 543,000 books,<sup id="cite_ref-observed_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observed-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:50</sup> the committee drew up a proposal for replacement of Gore in stages. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> was approached for financing without success.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[b]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Harry_Widener">Death of Harry Widener</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Widener_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Death of Harry Widener">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Elkins_Widener" title="Harry Elkins Widener">Harry Elkins Widener</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:92px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto.jpg" title="File:HarryElkinsWidener YearbookPhoto.jpg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg/90px-HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg" width="90" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg/135px-HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg/180px-HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="271" data-file-height="403" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarryElkinsWidener_YearbookPhoto_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Harry_Widener" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Widener">Harry Widener</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg/220px-HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg/330px-HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg/440px-HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2055" data-file-height="2077" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_GoreHall_RemovingBooks_c1912.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gore Hall was emptied via two electric trucks.<sup id="cite_ref-gazette2012A_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazette2012A-21">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1912, Harry Elkins Widener‍—‌scion of two of the wealthiest families in America,<sup id="cite_ref-dies_paris_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dies_paris-22">[20]</a></sup> a 1907 graduate of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_College" title="Harvard College">Harvard College</a>, and an accomplished <a href="/wiki/Book_collecting" title="Book collecting">bibliophile</a> despite his youth<sup id="cite_ref-newton_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newton-23">[21]</a></sup>‍—‌died in the <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_RMS_Titanic" title="Sinking of the RMS Titanic">sinking of the RMS <i>Titanic</i></a>. His father <a href="/wiki/George_Dunton_Widener" title="George Dunton Widener">George Dunton Widener</a> also perished, but his mother <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Elkins_Widener" title="Eleanor Elkins Widener">Eleanor Elkins Widener</a> survived.<sup id="cite_ref-dies_paris_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dies_paris-22">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harry Widener's will instructed that his mother, when "in her judgment <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> shall make arrange­ments for properly caring for my collec­tion of books<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[c]</a></sup><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... shall give them to said University to be known as the Harry Elkins Widener Collection",<sup id="cite_ref-HEW_will_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEW_will-27">[24]</a></sup> and he had told a friend, not long before he died, "I want to be remembered in connection with a great library, [but] I do not see how it is going to be brought about."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-newton_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newton-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>To enable the fulfillment of her son's wish Eleanor Widener briefly consid­ered funding an addition to Gore Hall, but soon determined to build instead a completely new and far larger library building‍—‌"a perpetual memorial"<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-canoe_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canoe-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:90</sup> to Harry Widener, housing not only his personal book collection but Harvard's general library as well,<sup id="cite_ref-gift_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gift-28">[25]</a></sup> with room for growth.<sup id="cite_ref-Harvard.27s_new_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harvard.27s_new-29">[26]</a></sup> As Biel has written, "The [Harvard architects] committee's <a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">Beaux Arts</a> design [for Gore Hall's projected replacement], with its massiveness and symmetry, offered monumen­tal­ity with nothing more particular to monumen­tal­ize than the aspira­tions of the modern university"‍—‌until the <i>Titanic</i> sank and "through delicate negotia­tion, [Harvard] convinced Eleanor Widener that the most eloquent tribute to Harry would be an entire library rather than a rare book wing."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-canoe_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canoe-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:88–9</sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terms_and_cost_of_gift">Terms and cost of gift</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Widener_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Terms and cost of gift">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To her gift Eleanor Widener attached a number of stipulations,<sup class="reference nowrap"><a href="#B">[B]</a>:43</sup> including that the building's architects be the firm of <a href="/wiki/Horace_Trumbauer" title="Horace Trumbauer">Horace Trumbauer<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>&amp; Associates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-valve_abele_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-valve_abele-30">[27]</a></sup> which had built several mansions for both the Elkins and the <a href="/wiki/Widener_family" title="Widener family">Widener</a> families.<sup class="reference nowrap"><a href="#B">[B]</a>:27</sup> "Mrs. Widener does not give the University the money to build a new library, but has offered to build a library satisfactory in external appearance to <i>herself,</i>" Harvard President <a href="/wiki/Abbott_Lawrence_Lowell" title="Abbott Lawrence Lowell">Abbott Lawrence Lowell</a> wrote privately. "The exterior was her own choice, and she has decided architec­tur­al opinions."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-shandtucci_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shandtucci-31">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:167</sup> Harvard historian <a href="/wiki/William_Bentinck-Smith" title="William Bentinck-Smith">William Bentinck-Smith</a> has written that</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913.jpg" title="File:GoreHallHarvard UnderDemolition early1913.jpg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg/290px-GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg" width="290" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg/435px-GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg/580px-GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="572" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GoreHallHarvard_UnderDemolition_early1913_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gore Hall under demolition</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>To [Harvard officials] Mrs. Widener was a lovely and generous lady whose wealth, power, and remoteness made her a somewhat terrifying figure who must not be roused to annoyance or outrage. Once [construction] began, all financial transactions were the donor's private business, and no one at Harvard ever knew the exact cost. Mrs. Widener was counting on $2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million, [but] it is probable the cost exceeded $3.5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million [equivalent to $540 million in 2016].<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[d]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Though Harvard awarded Trumbauer an honorary degree on the day of the new library's dedication,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[e]</a></sup> it was Trumbauer associate <a href="/wiki/Julian_F._Abele" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian F. Abele">Julian F. Abele</a> who had overall responsi­bility for the building's design,<sup id="cite_ref-valve_abele_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-valve_abele-30">[27]</a></sup> which largely followed the committee's outline (though with the committee's central circula­tion room shifted from the center to the northeast corner, yielding pride of place to the Memorial Rooms).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[f]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Gore Hall was turned into a "pile of stones and rubbish" to make way,<sup id="cite_ref-bentinck1980_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bentinck1980-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:13</sup> ground was broken on February<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>12, 1913, and the corner­stone laid on June<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>16. By later that year some 50,000 bricks were being laid each day.<sup id="cite_ref-gazette2012A_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazette2012A-21">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Building">Building</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Widener_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Building">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915.jpg" title="File:HarvardUniversity WidenerLibrary ExteriorFront c1915.jpg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg/220px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="103" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg/330px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg/440px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="811" data-file-height="380" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_ExteriorFront_c1915_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from <a href="/wiki/University_Hall_(Harvard_University)" title="University Hall (Harvard University)">University Hall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks.jpg" title="File:HarvardUniversity WidenerLibrary SecondFloorPlan SneadIronWorks.jpg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg/240px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg" width="240" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg/360px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg/480px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="631" data-file-height="797" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_SecondFloorPlan_SneadIronWorks_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Second floor plan (north at bottom)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At Harvard's "geographical and intellec­tual heart"<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-forrest_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forrest-40">[34]</a></sup> directly across <a href="/wiki/Tercentenary_Theatre_(Harvard_University)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tercentenary Theatre (Harvard University)">Tercenten­ary Theatre</a> from <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Church_of_Harvard_University" title="Memorial Church of Harvard University">Memorial Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bpl_sargent_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpl_sargent-41">[35]</a></sup> Widener Library is a hollow rectangle of "<a href="/wiki/Harvard_brick" title="Harvard brick">Harvard brick</a> with Indiana limestone <a href="/wiki/Traceries" class="mw-redirect" title="Traceries">traceries</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-stone_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stone-42">[36]</a></sup> 250 by 200 by 80<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>feet high (76 by 61 by 24<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m)<sup id="cite_ref-shandtucci_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shandtucci-31">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:167</sup> and enclosing 320,000 square feet (30,000<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-forrest_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forrest-40">[34]</a></sup>, "colon­naded on its front by immense pillars with elaborate <a href="/wiki/Capital_(architecture)#corinthian_capital" title="Capital (architecture)">[Corinthian capitals]</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AZ_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZ-43">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:362</sup> all of which stand at the head of a flight of stairs that would not disgrace the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">capitol in Washing­ton</a>."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-shandtucci_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shandtucci-31">[28]</a></sup> Sources describe the building's style as (variously) <a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">Beaux-Arts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-canoe_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canoe-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:88</sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-lacock_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lacock-44">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:57</sup><sup id="cite_ref-british_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-45">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:457</sup> <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellenistic architecture">Hellenistic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-whiffen_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whiffen-46">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:281</sup> or "the austere, formalistic <a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperial_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Imperial architecture (page does not exist)">Imperial</a> [or 'Imperial and Classical'] style displayed in the Law School's <a href="/wiki/Langdell_Hall" title="Langdell Hall">Langdell Hall</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Medical_School#Quadrangle" title="Harvard Medical School">Medical School Quadrangle</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-AZ_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZ-43">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:361</sup></p>
<p>The east, south, and west wings house the <a href="/wiki/Stacks_(library_architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stacks (library architecture)">stacks</a>, while the north contains administrative offices and various reading rooms, including the Main Reading Room (now the Loker Reading Room)‍—‌which, spanning the entire front of the building and some 42<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>feet (13<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m) in both depth and height, was termed by architec­tur­al historian <a href="/wiki/Bainbridge_Bunting" title="Bainbridge Bunting">Bainbridge Bunting</a> "the most ostenta­tious interior space at Harvard."<span class="Unicode nowrap"> </span><sup id="cite_ref-bunting_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bunting-47">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:154</sup> A topmost floor, supported by the stacks framework itself, contains thirty-two rooms for special collections, studies, offices, and seminars.<sup id="cite_ref-lane_libj_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lane_libj-48">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:327-8</sup></p>
<p>The Memorial Rooms (see <a href="#memorial_rooms">§ Widener Memorial Rooms</a>) are in the building's center, between what were originally two light courts (28 by 110<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>ft or 8.5 by 33<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>m)<sup id="cite_ref-potter_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-potter-49">[43]</a></sup> (now enclosed as additional reading rooms).<sup id="cite_ref-potier_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-potier-50">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dedication">Dedication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Widener_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Dedication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg/180px-HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg" width="180" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg/270px-HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg/360px-HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="587" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarryElkinsWidener_portrait_by_GabrielFerrier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Ferrier" title="Gabriel Ferrier">Gabriel Ferrier</a>'s por­trait of Harry Widener hangs in the Memorial Rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-ask_portrait_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ask_portrait-51">[45]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The building was dedicated immediately after <a href="/wiki/History_and_traditions_of_Harvard_commencements" title="History and traditions of Harvard commencements">Com­mence­ment Day</a> exercises on June<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>24, 1915. Lowell and Coolidge mounted the steps to the main door, where Eleanor Widener presented them with the building's keys.<sup id="cite_ref-dedication_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dedication-52">[46]</a></sup> The first book formally brought into the new library was the 1634 edition of <a href="/wiki/John_Downame" title="John Downame">John Downame</a>'s <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Christian_Warfare_Against_the_Devil,_World,_and_Flesh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Christian Warfare Against the Devil, World, and Flesh (page does not exist)">The Christian Warfare Against the Devil, World, and Flesh</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-bentinck1980_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bentinck1980-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:18</sup> believed (at the time) to be the only volume, of those bequeathed to the school by <a href="/wiki/John_Harvard_(clergyman)" title="John Harvard (clergyman)">John Harvard</a> in 1636, to have survived the 1754 burning of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Hall_(Harvard_University)" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard Hall (Harvard University)">Harvard Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tomase_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tomase-53">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png/240px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png" width="240" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png/360px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png/480px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_Dedication.png 2x" data-file-width="672" data-file-height="479" /></a>

</div>
</div>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg/240px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg" width="240" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg/360px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg/480px-HarvardUniversity_WidenerLibrary_StairsToMemorialRooms.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2379" data-file-height="2227" /></a>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
